     <p>
      <b>
       Sir Stirling Craufurd Moss
      </b>
      ,
      <span style="font-size:100%;">
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">
        OBE
       </a>
      </span>
      (born 17 September 1929) is a British former
      <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">
       Formula One
      </a>
      racing driver. An inductee into the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Motorsports_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Motorsports Hall of Fame">
       International Motorsports Hall of Fame
      </a>
      , he achieved success in several categories of competition and has been described as "the greatest driver never to win the World Championship".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grandprixcom_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-grandprixcom-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">
       Early life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Moss was born in London, the son of Aileen (ne Craufurd) and
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Moss" title="Alfred Moss">
       Alfred Moss
      </a>
      , a dentist of
      <a href="/wiki/Bray,_Berkshire" title="Bray, Berkshire">
       Bray, Berkshire
      </a>
      , where Stirling was raised at
      <i>
       Long White Cloud
      </i>
      house on the right bank of the
      <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">
       River Thames
      </a>
      . Alfred was an amateur racing driver who had been placed 16th at the
      <a href="/wiki/1924_Indianapolis_500" title="1924 Indianapolis 500">
       1924 Indianapolis 500
      </a>
      . Stirling was a gifted horse rider as was his younger sister,
      <a href="/wiki/Pat_Moss" title="Pat Moss">
       Pat Moss
      </a>
      , who became a successful
      <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">
       rally driver
      </a>
      and married
      <a href="/wiki/Erik_Carlsson" title="Erik Carlsson">
       Erik Carlsson
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss was educated at independent schools;
      <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_House_School" title="Shrewsbury House School">
       Shrewsbury House School
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Surbiton" title="Surbiton">
       Surbiton
      </a>
      ) Clewer Manor Junior School and the linked senior school
      <a href="/wiki/Haileybury_and_Imperial_Service_College" title="Haileybury and Imperial Service College">
       Haileybury and Imperial Service College
      </a>
      . All were for boys (but the latter are now co-educational except for Shrewsbury) and located at
      <a href="/wiki/Hertford_Heath" title="Hertford Heath">
       Hertford Heath
      </a>
      , near
      <a href="/wiki/Hertford" title="Hertford">
       Hertford
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Racing_career">
       Racing career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Racing career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="951" data-file-width="1285" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg/220px-Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg/330px-Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg/440px-Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanwall_VW5_Aintree_1957.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Moss shared this
        <a href="/wiki/Vanwall" title="Vanwall">
         Vanwall
        </a>
        VW5 with
        <a href="/wiki/Tony_Brooks" title="Tony Brooks">
         Tony Brooks
        </a>
        to win the
        <a href="/wiki/1957_British_Grand_Prix" title="1957 British Grand Prix">
         1957 British Grand Prix
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Moss, who raced from 1948 to 1962, won 212 of the 529 races he entered, including 16
      <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">
       Formula One
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_motor_racing" title="Grand Prix motor racing">
       Grands Prix
      </a>
      . He would compete in as many as 62 races in a single year and drove 84 different makes of car over the course of his racing career, including
      <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Car_Company" title="Cooper Car Company">
       Cooper 500
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/English_Racing_Automobiles#G-Type" title="English Racing Automobiles">
       ERA
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rob_Walker_Racing_Team" title="Rob Walker Racing Team">
       Lotus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Maserati_250F" title="Maserati 250F">
       Maserati
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_W196" title="Mercedes-Benz W196">
       Mercedes-Benz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Porsche_718" title="Porsche 718">
       Porsche
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Vanwall" title="Vanwall">
       Vanwall
      </a>
      single-seaters,
      <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DBR1" title="Aston Martin DBR1">
       Aston Martin
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maserati_300,_450,_Tipo_61&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maserati 300, 450, Tipo 61 (page does not exist)">
       Maserati
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_250#250_GT_Berlinetta_SWB" title="Ferrari 250">
       Ferrari
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_C-Type" title="Jaguar C-Type">
       Jaguar
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_300_SLR" title="Mercedes-Benz 300 SLR">
       Mercedes-Benz
      </a>
      sports cars, and
      <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Mark_VII" title="Jaguar Mark VII">
       Jaguar
      </a>
      saloons. Like many drivers of the era, he competed in several formulae, often on the same day.
     </p>
     <p>
      He preferred to race British cars, stating, "Better to lose honourably in a British car than win in a foreign one".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-motorsportshalloffame.com_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-motorsportshalloffame.com-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At Vanwall, he was instrumental in breaking the German/Italian stranglehold on F1 racing (as was
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brabham" title="Jack Brabham">
       Jack Brabham
      </a>
      at Cooper). He remained the English driver with the most Formula One victories until 1991 when
      <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Mansell" title="Nigel Mansell">
       Nigel Mansell
      </a>
      overtook him after competing in more races.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1948.E2.80.931954">
       19481954
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19481954">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      One of the Cooper Car Company's first customers, Moss used winnings from competing in horse-riding events to pay the deposit on a Cooper 500 racing car in 1948. He then persuaded his father, who opposed his racing and wanted him to be a dentist, to let him buy it. He soon demonstrated his ability with numerous wins at national and international levels, and continued to compete in
      <a href="/wiki/Formula_Three" title="Formula Three">
       Formula Three
      </a>
      , with Coopers and
      <a href="/wiki/Kieft_Cars" title="Kieft Cars">
       Kiefts
      </a>
      , after he had progressed to more senior categories.
     </p>
     <p>
      His first major international race victory came on the eve of his 21st birthday at the wheel of a borrowed
      <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_XK120" title="Jaguar XK120">
       Jaguar XK120
      </a>
      in the 1950
      <a href="/wiki/RAC_Tourist_Trophy" title="RAC Tourist Trophy">
       RAC Tourist Trophy
      </a>
      on the
      <a href="/wiki/Dundrod" title="Dundrod">
       Dundrod
      </a>
      circuit in Northern Ireland. He went on to win the race six more times, in 1951 (Jaguar C-Type), 1955 (Mercedes-Benz 300SLR), 1958 and 1959 (Aston Martin DBR1), and 1960 and 1961 (Ferrari 250 GT).
     </p>
     <p>
      Also a competent rally driver, he is one of three people to have won a
      <i>
       Coupe d'Or
      </i>
      (Gold Cup) for three consecutive penalty-free runs on the
      <a href="/wiki/Alpine_Rally" title="Alpine Rally">
       Alpine Rally
      </a>
      (Coupe des Alpes). He finished second in the 1952
      <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="Monte Carlo Rally">
       Monte Carlo Rally
      </a>
      driving a
      <a href="/wiki/Sunbeam-Talbot_90" title="Sunbeam-Talbot 90">
       Sunbeam-Talbot 90
      </a>
      with Desmond Scannell and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Autocar" title="Autocar">
        Autocar
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine editor John Cooper as co-drivers.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1954, he became the first non-American to win the
      <a href="/wiki/12_Hours_of_Sebring" title="12 Hours of Sebring">
       12 Hours of Sebring
      </a>
      , sharing the
      <a href="/wiki/Briggs_Cunningham" title="Briggs Cunningham">
       Cunningham
      </a>
      team's 1.5-liter O.S.C.A. MT4 with American Bill Lloyd.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1953 Mercedes-Benz racing boss
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Neubauer" title="Alfred Neubauer">
       Alfred Neubauer
      </a>
      had spoken to Moss's manager, Ken Gregory, about the possibility of Moss's joining the Mercedes Grand Prix team. Having seen him do well in a relatively uncompetitive car, and wanting to see how he would perform in a better one, Neubauer suggested Moss buy a Maserati for the 1954 season. He bought a
      <a href="/wiki/Maserati_250F" title="Maserati 250F">
       Maserati 250F
      </a>
      , and although the car's unreliability prevented his scoring high points in the 1954
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Drivers%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Drivers' Champions">
       Drivers' Championship
      </a>
      he qualified alongside the Mercedes frontrunners several times and performed well in the races.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/1954_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="1954 Italian Grand Prix">
       Italian Grand Prix
      </a>
      at Monza he passed both drivers who were regarded as the best in Formula One at the time
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Fangio" title="Juan Manuel Fangio">
       Juan Manuel Fangio
      </a>
      in a Mercedes and
      <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Ascari" title="Alberto Ascari">
       Alberto Ascari
      </a>
      in a Ferrariand took the lead. Ascari retired with engine problems, and Moss led until lap 68 when his engine also failed. Fangio took the victory, and Moss pushed his Maserati to the finish line. Neubauer, already impressed when Moss had tested a
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_W196" title="Mercedes-Benz W196">
       Mercedes-Benz W196
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Hockenheimring" title="Hockenheimring">
       Hockenheim
      </a>
      , promptly signed him for 1955.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1955">
       1955
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1955">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Moss's first Formula One victory was in the
      <a href="/wiki/1955_British_Grand_Prix" title="1955 British Grand Prix">
       1955 British Grand Prix
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Aintree_Motor_Racing_Circuit" title="Aintree Motor Racing Circuit">
       Aintree
      </a>
      , a race he was also the first British driver to win. Leading a 1234 finish for Mercedes, it was the first time he beat Fangio, his teammate and arch rival, who was also his friend and mentor. It has been suggested that Fangio sportingly allowed Moss to win in front of his home crowd. Moss himself asked Fangio repeatedly, and Fangio always replied: "No. You were just better than me that day."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The same year, Moss also won the RAC Tourist Trophy, the
      <a href="/wiki/Targa_Florio" title="Targa Florio">
       Targa Florio
      </a>
      (sharing the drive with
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Collins_(racing_driver)" title="Peter Collins (racing driver)">
       Peter Collins
      </a>
      ), and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mille_Miglia" title="Mille Miglia">
       Mille Miglia
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mille_Miglia">
       Mille Miglia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mille Miglia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In 1955 Moss won Italy's thousand-mile
      <a href="/wiki/1955_Mille_Miglia" title="1955 Mille Miglia">
       Mille Miglia
      </a>
      road race, an achievement
      <a href="/wiki/Doug_Nye" title="Doug Nye">
       Doug Nye
      </a>
      described as the "most iconic single day's drive in motor racing history."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nye_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nye-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Motor_Trend" title="Motor Trend">
        Motor Trend
       </a>
      </i>
      headlined it as "The Most Epic Drive. Ever."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss, then 25 years old, drove one of four factory-entered
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_300_SLR" title="Mercedes-Benz 300 SLR">
       Mercedes-Benz 300 SLR
      </a>
      sports-racing cars. Based on the W196 Grand Prix car, they had
      <a href="/wiki/Space_frame" title="Space frame">
       spaceframe
      </a>
      chassis and
      <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_alloy" title="Magnesium alloy">
       magnesium-alloy
      </a>
      bodies, and their modified W196 engines ran on a mixture of petrol,
      <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">
       benzene
      </a>
      , and alcohol. The team's main race rivals were the factory-entered Ferraris of
      <a href="/wiki/Piero_Taruffi" title="Piero Taruffi">
       Piero Taruffi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Castellotti" title="Eugenio Castellotti">
       Eugenio Castellotti
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Maglioli" title="Umberto Maglioli">
       Umberto Maglioli
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Paolo_Marzotto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Paolo Marzotto (page does not exist)">
       Paolo Marzotto
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Journalist
      <a href="/wiki/Denis_Jenkinson" title="Denis Jenkinson">
       Denis Jenkinson
      </a>
      was Moss's navigator. He had intended to go with
      <a href="/wiki/John_Fitch_(racing_driver)" title="John Fitch (racing driver)">
       John Fitch
      </a>
      , whose idea it had been to take a navigator, but when Mercedes assigned a
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_300SL" title="Mercedes-Benz 300SL">
       300 SL
      </a>
      to Fitch, the American agreed to Jenkinson riding with Moss in the faster SLR. Jenkinson had come up with the idea of
      <a href="/wiki/Pacenotes" title="Pacenotes">
       pace notes
      </a>
      in the form of a roller map of the route on which he had noted its hazardsan innovation that helped Moss compete against drivers with greater local knowledge. Jenkinson used hand signals to tell him about the road ahead. Radio communication had proved ineffective when they tried it, because when Moss was fully concentrated on his driving he was oblivious to Jenkinson's voice.
     </p>
     <p>
      Fangio, who regarded the race as too dangerous for passengers, drove his SLR alone, as did
      <a href="/wiki/Karl_Kling" title="Karl Kling">
       Karl Kling
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Herrmann" title="Hans Herrmann">
       Hans Herrmann
      </a>
      drove the fourth car with mechanic Herman Eger as passenger.
     </p>
     <p>
      The race was a timed event, and competitors started singly at one-minute intervals. Moss's Mercedes left the starting ramp in
      <a href="/wiki/Brescia" title="Brescia">
       Brescia
      </a>
      at 7:22a.m. (hence the car's race number 722). Castellotti's Ferrari left one minute later, and Taruffi's at 7:27.
     </p>
     <p>
      After about 90 miles, as Moss approached
      <a href="/wiki/Padua" title="Padua">
       Padua
      </a>
      at 175mph (282km/h) he saw in his mirror that Castellotti was closing fast. When Moss misjudged a corner and collided with some straw bales Castellotti went past and built an increasing lead. After 188 miles of racing the Italian had to stop in
      <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">
       Ravenna
      </a>
      to replace the Ferrari's tyres, and fell behind again. Marzotto's Ferrari started well but the tread separated from a tyre at over 170mph (274km/h) and he had to withdraw from the race because the spare turned out to be the wrong size.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nearing the Adriatic coast, Jenkinson's spectacles were blown off by the slipstream when he vomited over the side of the Mercedes; he carried a replacement pair. Arriving in Rome, he and Moss were told they were leading from Taruffi, Herrmann, Kling and Fangio, but from then on they had no way of knowing whether any of their rivals had gone ahead on elapsed time. Soon after Rome, Kling's race ended when he went off the road avoiding spectators and crashed into a tree.
     </p>
     <p>
      When Moss and Jenkinson finally arrived at the finish in Brescia they learned that Castellotti's Ferrari had retired with transmission trouble and they had won. Fangio took second place, nearly 33 minutes slower, his Mercedes delayed by engine trouble and running on only seven cylinders by the end. Maglioli, in the sole surviving factory-entered Ferrari, took 45 minutes longer than Moss and finished 3rd.
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss's time of 10 hours, 7 minutes and 48 seconds, and his average speed of 98.53mph (159km/h) for the 1000 miles, set course records that still stand. The race was discontinued two years later.
     </p>
     <p>
      Before the race, he had taken a "magic pill" given him by Fangio, and he has commented that although he did not know what was in it, "Dexedrine and Benzedrine were commonly used in rallies. The object was simply to keep awake, like wartime bomber crews." After the win, he spent the night and the following day driving his girlfriend to Cologne, stopping for breakfast in Munich and lunch in Stuttgart.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nye_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nye-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1956.E2.80.931962">
       19561962
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 19561962">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="832" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg/220px-Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg/330px-Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg/440px-Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moss_and_Ireland_at_1961_Dutch_Grand_Prix.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Moss (left) with
        <a href="/wiki/Innes_Ireland" title="Innes Ireland">
         Innes Ireland
        </a>
        in 1961
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Moss won the Nassau Cup at the 1956 and 1957
      <a href="/wiki/Bahamas_Speed_Week" title="Bahamas Speed Week">
       Bahamas Speed Week
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-si19601212_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-si19601212-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also in 1957 he won on the longest circuit ever to hold a World Championship Grand Prix, the 25km (16mi)
      <a href="/wiki/Pescara_Circuit" title="Pescara Circuit">
       Pescara Circuit
      </a>
      , where he again demonstrated his mastery of long-distance racing. The event lasted three hours and Moss beat Fangio, who started from
      <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">
       pole position
      </a>
      , by a little over 3 minutes.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1958 Moss won the first race in a rear-engined F1 car. Within two years all car featured this design.
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss's sporting attitude cost him the 1958 Formula 1 World Championship. When rival
      <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hawthorn" title="Mike Hawthorn">
       Mike Hawthorn
      </a>
      was threatened with a penalty after the
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Grand_Prix" title="Portuguese Grand Prix">
       Portuguese Grand Prix
      </a>
      , Moss defended him. Hawthorn was accused of reversing on the track after spinning and stalling his car on an uphill section. Moss had shouted advice to Hawthorn to steer downhill, against traffic, to bump-start the car. Moss's quick thinking, and his defence of Hawthorn before the stewards, preserved Hawthorn's 6 points for finishing second behind Moss. Hawthorn went on to beat Moss for the championship title by one point, even though he had won only one race that year to Moss's four.
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss was as gifted in sports cars as in Grand Prix cars. To his victories in the Tourist Trophy, the Sebring 12 Hours and the Mille Miglia he added three consecutive wins (19581960) in the gruelling
      <a href="/wiki/1000_km_N%C3%BCrburgring" title="1000 km Nrburgring">
       1000 km Nrburgring
      </a>
      , the first two in an
      <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">
       Aston Martin
      </a>
      (in which he did most of the driving) and the third in a
      <a href="/wiki/Maserati_Tipo_61" title="Maserati Tipo 61">
       Tipo
       <i>
        61
       </i>
      </a>
      "birdcage"
      <a href="/wiki/Maserati_in_motorsport" title="Maserati in motorsport">
       Maserati
      </a>
      , co-driving with the American
      <a href="/wiki/Dan_Gurney" title="Dan Gurney">
       Dan Gurney
      </a>
      . The pair lost nearly six minutes when an oil hose blew off, but despite miserable conditions they made up the time and took 1st place.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1960 Formula One season, Moss won the
      <a href="/wiki/1960_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="1960 Monaco Grand Prix">
       Monaco Grand Prix
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rob_Walker_(motorsport)" title="Rob Walker (motorsport)">
       Rob Walker
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coventry-Climax" title="Coventry-Climax">
       Coventry-Climax
      </a>
      -powered
      <a href="/wiki/Lotus_18" title="Lotus 18">
       Lotus 18
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Seriously injured in an accident at the Burnenville curve during practice for the
      <a href="/wiki/1960_Belgian_Grand_Prix" title="1960 Belgian Grand Prix">
       Belgian Grand Prix
      </a>
      at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spa-Francorchamps" title="Spa-Francorchamps">
       Spa-Francorchamps
      </a>
      , he missed the next three races but recovered sufficiently to win the final one of the season, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Grand_Prix" title="United States Grand Prix">
       United States Grand Prix
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Riverside_International_Raceway" title="Riverside International Raceway">
       Riverside
      </a>
      , California.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="680" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg/220px-MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg/330px-MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg/440px-MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MossLotusClimax19610806.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Moss at the
        <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="Nrburgring">
         Nrburgring
        </a>
        in 1961
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      For the 1961 Formula One season, run under new 1.5-litre rules,
      <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Ferrari" title="Enzo Ferrari">
       Enzo Ferrari
      </a>
      fielded the "sharknose"
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferrari_156" title="Ferrari 156">
       Ferrari 156
      </a>
      with an all-new
      <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">
       V6 engine
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Moss's Climax-engined
      <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">
       Lotus
      </a>
      was comparatively underpowered, but he won the
      <a href="/wiki/1961_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="1961 Monaco Grand Prix">
       1961 Monaco Grand Prix
      </a>
      by 3.6 seconds, beating the Ferraris of
      <a href="/wiki/Richie_Ginther" title="Richie Ginther">
       Richie Ginther
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_von_Trips" title="Wolfgang von Trips">
       Wolfgang von Trips
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Phil_Hill" title="Phil Hill">
       Phil Hill
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_11-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and went on to win the partially wet
      <a href="/wiki/1961_German_Grand_Prix" title="1961 German Grand Prix">
       1961 German Grand Prix
      </a>
      . In addition to his skill, two other factors helped compensate for the Lotus's power deficit in these races. The tight circuit at Monaco favored the nimble Lotus, countering the horsepower advantage of the heavier, ill-handling Ferraris; and at the Nrburgring, Moss and manager Ken Gregory took the risky decision to fit rain tyres after a pre-race shower soaked the track. Had the skies cleared and the track dried, the decision would have worked against Moss. The rain returned in the race, and although Moss's tyres rapidly deteriorated he was able to drive away from Hill and Trips to take the win.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1962, he crashed his Lotus heavily during the
      <a href="/wiki/1962_Glover_Trophy" title="1962 Glover Trophy">
       Glover Trophy
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Goodwood_Circuit" title="Goodwood Circuit">
       Goodwood
      </a>
      held on Monday 15 April. The accident put him in a coma for a month, and for six months the left side of his body was partially paralysed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-motorsportshalloffame.com_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-motorsportshalloffame.com-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He recovered, but retired from professional racing after a private test session in a
      <a href="/wiki/Lotus_19" title="Lotus 19">
       Lotus 19
      </a>
      the following year, when he lapped a few tenths of a second slower than before. He felt he had not regained his previously instinctive command of the car. He had been runner-up in the Drivers' Championship four years in succession, from 1955 to 1958, and third in each of the next three years.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Record-breaking">
       Record-breaking
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Record-breaking">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In the 1950s Moss participated in several successful speed record attempts.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1950">
       1950
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1950">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      At the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autodrome_de_Montlh%C3%A9ry" title="Autodrome de Montlhry">
       Autodrome de Montlhry
      </a>
      , a steeply banked oval track near
      <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
       Paris
      </a>
      , Moss and
      <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Johnson_(racing_driver)" title="Leslie Johnson (racing driver)">
       Leslie Johnson
      </a>
      took turns at the wheel of the latter's
      <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_XK120" title="Jaguar XK120">
       Jaguar XK120
      </a>
      to average 107.46mph (172.94km/h) for 24hours, including stops for fuel and tyres. Changing drivers every three hours, they covered a total of 2579.16 miles. It was the first time a production car had averaged over 100mph (160.93km/h) for 24 hours.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg/220px-Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg/330px-Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg/440px-Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jaguar_XK120_%27Montlhery%27_FHC_-_Flickr_-_exfordy.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Record-breaking 1952 Jaguar XK120, seen in 2008
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1952">
       1952
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1952">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Revisiting Montlhry, Moss was one of a four-driver team, led by Johnson, who drove a factory-owned Jaguar XK120 fixed-head coup for 7days and nights at the French track.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Moss, Johnson, Bert Hadley and
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Fairman" title="Jack Fairman">
       Jack Fairman
      </a>
      averaged 100.31mph (161.43km/h) to take four World records and five International Class C records, and covered a total of 16,851.73mi (27,120.23km).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1957">
       1957
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1957">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In August Moss broke five International Class F records in the purpose-built MG EX181 at
      <a href="/wiki/Bonneville_Salt_Flats" title="Bonneville Salt Flats">
       Bonneville Salt Flats
      </a>
      . The streamlined, supercharged car's speed for the flying kilometer was 245.64mph, which was the average of two runs in opposite directions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting_career">
       Broadcasting career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Broadcasting career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Away from driving, in 1962 he acted as a
      <a href="/wiki/Color_commentator" title="Color commentator">
       colour commentator
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
       ABC's
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wide_World_of_Sports_(US_TV_series)" title="Wide World of Sports (US TV series)">
       Wide World of Sports
      </a>
      for Formula One and NASCAR races. He eventually left ABC in 1980.
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss narrated the official
      <a href="/wiki/1988_Formula_One_season" title="1988 Formula One season">
       1988 Formula One season review
      </a>
      along with
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Jardine" title="Tony Jardine">
       Tony Jardine
      </a>
      . Moss also narrated the popular children's series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Roary_the_Racing_Car" title="Roary the Racing Car">
        Roary the Racing Car
       </a>
      </i>
      , which stars
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kay" title="Peter Kay">
       Peter Kay
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_racing">
       Return to racing
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Return to racing">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StirlingMoss.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/StirlingMoss.jpg/220px-StirlingMoss.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/StirlingMoss.jpg/330px-StirlingMoss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/StirlingMoss.jpg/440px-StirlingMoss.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StirlingMoss.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Sir Stirling Moss racing an
        <a href="/wiki/O.S.C.A." title="O.S.C.A.">
         OSCA
        </a>
        MT4 Spider
        <a href="/wiki/Morelli_(company)" title="Morelli (company)">
         Morelli
        </a>
        at Speed, 2006
        <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Classic" title="Silverstone Classic">
         Silverstone Classic
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
         <a href="#cite_note-15">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          15
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silverstone_circuit" title="Silverstone circuit">
         Silverstone circuit
        </a>
        , England. 29 July 2006.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2073" data-file-width="3166" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg/220px-OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg/330px-OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg/440px-OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OSCA_FS372_Moss_in_Bahamas.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Sir Stirling Moss demonstrating his
        <a href="/wiki/O.S.C.A." title="O.S.C.A.">
         OSCA FS372
        </a>
        Spider
        <a href="/wiki/Morelli_(company)" title="Morelli (company)">
         Morelli
        </a>
        at the 2011
        <a href="/wiki/Bahamas_Speed_Week" title="Bahamas Speed Week">
         Bahamas Speed Week
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
         <a href="#cite_note-16">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          16
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="709" data-file-width="1176" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg/220px-Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg/330px-Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg/440px-Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mercedes_SLR_Stirling_Moss_1977.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Sir Stirling Moss demonstrating a 300 SLR at the
        <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="Nrburgring">
         Nrburgring
        </a>
        in 1977
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Although ostensibly retired from racing since 1962, Moss did make a number of one-off appearances in professional motorsport events in the following two decades. He also competed in the
      <a href="/wiki/1974_London-Sahara-Munich_World_Cup_Rally" title="1974 London-Sahara-Munich World Cup Rally">
       1974 London-Sahara-Munich World Cup Rally
      </a>
      in a Mercedes-Benz, but retired from the event in the Algerian Sahara.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Holden_Torana" title="Holden Torana">
       Holden Torana
      </a>
      he shared with
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brabham" title="Jack Brabham">
       Jack Brabham
      </a>
      in the 1976
      <a href="/wiki/Bathurst_1000" title="Bathurst 1000">
       Bathurst 1000
      </a>
      was hit from behind on the grid and eventually retired with engine failure. Moss, at the wheel of the Torana when the
      <a href="/wiki/Holden_V8_engine" title="Holden V8 engine">
       V8 engine
      </a>
      let go, was criticised by other drivers for staying on the racing line for over  of the 6.172km long circuit while returning to the pits as the car was dropping large amounts of oil onto the road.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also shared a
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">
       Volkswagen Golf
      </a>
      GTI with
      <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hulme" title="Denny Hulme">
       Denny Hulme
      </a>
      in the 1979 Benson &amp; Hedges 500 at
      <a href="/wiki/Pukekohe_Park_Raceway" title="Pukekohe Park Raceway">
       Pukekohe Park Raceway
      </a>
      in New Zealand.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1980 he made a comeback to regular competition, in the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">
       British Saloon Car Championship
      </a>
      with the works-backed GTi Engineering
      <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">
       Audi
      </a>
      team.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoodMen_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GoodMen-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the 1980 season Moss was the team's number two driver to team co-owner
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lloyd_(racing_driver)" title="Richard Lloyd (racing driver)">
       Richard Lloyd
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RacingGolfs_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RacingGolfs-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the 1981 season Moss stayed with Audi, as the team moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Walkinshaw_Racing" title="Tom Walkinshaw Racing">
       Tom Walkinshaw Racing
      </a>
      management, driving alongside
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Brundle" title="Martin Brundle">
       Martin Brundle
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Throughout his retirement he raced in events for historic cars, driving on behalf of and at the invitation of others, as well as campaigning his own
      <a href="/wiki/O.S.C.A." title="O.S.C.A.">
       OSCA
      </a>
      FS372 and other vehicles.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 9 June 2011 during qualifying for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le_Mans_Legends" title="Le Mans Legends">
       Le Mans Legends
      </a>
      race, Moss announced on
      <a href="/wiki/Radio_Le_Mans" title="Radio Le Mans">
       Radio Le Mans
      </a>
      that he had finally retired from racing, saying that he had scared himself that afternoon. He was 81.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="After_his_racing_career">
       After his racing career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: After his racing career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In June 2005 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Goodwood_Festival_of_Speed" title="Goodwood Festival of Speed">
       Goodwood Festival of Speed
      </a>
      Moss signed the bonnet of his 1955
      <a href="/wiki/Mille_Miglia" title="Mille Miglia">
       Mille Miglia
      </a>
      -winning
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_300_SLR" title="Mercedes-Benz 300 SLR">
       Mercedes-Benz 300 SLR
      </a>
      . It was the car's final public appearance before retiring to the newly built
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Museum" title="Mercedes-Benz Museum">
       Mercedes-Benz Museum
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">
       Stuttgart
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Although occasionally an outspoken critic of
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Schumacher" title="Michael Schumacher">
       Michael Schumacher
      </a>
      , in October 2006 Moss ranked him joint fourth with
      <a href="/wiki/Tazio_Nuvolari" title="Tazio Nuvolari">
       Tazio Nuvolari
      </a>
      in the pantheon of all-time greats, behind
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Fangio" title="Juan Manuel Fangio">
       Juan Manuel Fangio
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">
       Ayrton Senna
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Jim_Clark" title="Jim Clark">
       Jim Clark
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss's 80th birthday, on 17 September 2009, fell on the eve of the
      <a href="/wiki/Goodwood_Revival" title="Goodwood Revival">
       Goodwood Revival
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Gordon-Lennox,_Earl_of_March_and_Kinrara" title="Charles Gordon-Lennox, Earl of March and Kinrara">
       Lord March
      </a>
      celebrated with an 80-car parade on each of the three days. Moss drove a different car each day: a Mercedes W196
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monoposto" title="Monoposto">
        Monoposto
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Lotus_18" title="Lotus 18">
       Lotus 18
      </a>
      in which he had won the 1961 Monaco GP, and an
      <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DBR3" title="Aston Martin DBR3">
       Aston Martin DBR3
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 7 March 2010 he broke both ankles and four bones in a foot, and also chipped four vertebrae and suffered skin lesions, when he fell down a lift shaft at his home.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Recovered from his injuries, he appeared in a pre-race BBC interview at the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_British_Grand_Prix" title="2010 British Grand Prix">
       2010 British Grand Prix
      </a>
      meeting at Silverstone and presented
      <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">
       Lewis Hamilton
      </a>
      with his second-place trophy on the podium.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">
       Honours
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Honours">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      He was the subject of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/This_Is_Your_Life_(UK_TV_series)" title="This Is Your Life (UK TV series)">
        This Is Your Life
       </a>
      </i>
      in 1959 when he was surprised by
      <a href="/wiki/Eamonn_Andrews" title="Eamonn Andrews">
       Eamonn Andrews
      </a>
      at the BBC Television Theatre.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1990, Moss was inducted into the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Motorsports_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Motorsports Hall of Fame">
       International Motorsports Hall of Fame
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Year_Honours_2000" title="New Year Honours 2000">
       New Year Honours 2000
      </a>
      List, Moss was made a
      <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">
       Knight Bachelor
      </a>
      for services to motor racing. On 21 March 2000, he was knighted by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" title="Prince Charles">
       Prince Charles
      </a>
      , standing in for the Queen, who was on an official visit to Australia. As Moss drove his Mercedes away from Buckingham Palace after the ceremony, he was stopped by a palace guard who joked: "Who do you think you are? Stirling Moss?" Moss smiled and replied "Sir Stirling Moss, actually."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He received the 2005
      <a href="/wiki/Segrave_Trophy" title="Segrave Trophy">
       Segrave Trophy
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2006, Moss was awarded the FIA gold medal in recognition of his outstanding contribution to motorsport.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In December 2008,
      <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">
       McLaren
      </a>
      -
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">
       Mercedes
      </a>
      unveiled their final model of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_SLR_McLaren" title="Mercedes-Benz SLR McLaren">
       Mercedes-Benz SLR McLaren
      </a>
      . The model was named in honour of Stirling Moss, hence,
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_SLR_McLaren#Stirling_Moss_.282009.29" title="Mercedes-Benz SLR McLaren">
       Mercedes McLaren SLR Stirling Moss
      </a>
      , which has a top speed of 217mph (349km/h) with wind deflectors instead of a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windscreen" title="Windscreen">
       windscreen
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Moss.27s_biography">
       Moss's biography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Moss's biography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1963, noted
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorsports" title="Motorsports">
       motorsports
      </a>
      author and commentator
      <a href="/wiki/Ken_Purdy" title="Ken Purdy">
       Ken Purdy
      </a>
      published a biographical book entitled
      <i>
       All But My Life
      </i>
      about Stirling Moss (first published by William Kimber &amp; Co., Ltd., London), based on material gathered through interviews with Moss.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">
       Popular culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Popular culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During his driving career, Moss was one of the most recognised celebrities in Britain, leading to many media appearances. In March 1958, Moss was a guest challenger on the TV panel show "What's My Line?" (episode with Anita Ekberg). He was interviewed by
      <a href="/wiki/John_Freeman_(British_politician)" title="John Freeman (British politician)">
       John Freeman
      </a>
      on the interview series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Face_to_Face_(British_TV_series)" title="Face to Face (British TV series)">
        Face to Face
       </a>
      </i>
      , broadcast on 12 June 1960; Freeman later said that he had thought before the interview that Moss was a playboy, but in their meeting he showed cold, precise, clinical judgement... a man who could live so close to the edge of death and danger, and trust entirely to his own judgement. This appealed to me.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He appeared as himself in the 1964 film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Beauty_Jungle" title="The Beauty Jungle">
        The Beauty Jungle
       </a>
      </i>
      , and was also one of the celebrities who made cameo appearances in the 1967 version of the
      <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">
       James Bond
      </a>
      film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(1967_film)" title="Casino Royale (1967 film)">
        Casino Royale
       </a>
      </i>
      . He played Evelyn Tremble's (
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">
       Peter Sellers
      </a>
      ) driver.
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 1960, Moss was fined 50 and his driving licence revoked for a year after he was convicted of dangerous driving.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ban_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ban-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Moss, test-driving a new Austin Seven in Shropshire, had collided with an oncoming van when overtaking a Rover car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For many years during and after his career, the rhetorical phrase "Who do you think you are, Stirling Moss?" was supposedly the standard question all British policemen asked speeding motorists. Moss relates he himself was once stopped for speeding and asked just that; he reports the traffic officer had some difficulty believing him.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As related in the book
      <i>
       The Life and Times of Private Eye
      </i>
      , Moss was the subject of a less than respectful cartoon biography in the magazine
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_Eye_(magazine)" title="Private Eye (magazine)">
        Private Eye
       </a>
      </i>
      . The cartoon, drawn by
      <a href="/wiki/Willie_Rushton" title="Willie Rushton">
       Willie Rushton
      </a>
      , showed him continually crashing, having his driving licence revoked and finally "hosting television programmes on subjects he knows nothing about". It also made reference to the amnesia Moss suffered from as a result of head injuries sustained in the crash at Goodwood in 1962. According to the book, Moss responded by offering to buy the original of the cartoon, an outcome the book describes as "depressingly common" for its satirical cartoons about famous people.
     </p>
     <p>
      Moss is the narrator of the popular children's series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Roary_the_Racing_Car" title="Roary the Racing Car">
        Roary the Racing Car
       </a>
      </i>
      which stars
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kay" title="Peter Kay">
       Peter Kay
      </a>
      , a role he took on, having being approached by both David Jenkins, who had the original idea, and Keith Chapman, the later the creator of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bob_the_Builder" title="Bob the Builder">
        Bob the Builder
       </a>
      </i>
      , as he saw the TV show as a way of introducing motorsport to the next generation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He is one of the few drivers of his era to create a brand from his name for licensing purposes, which was launched when his website was revamped in 2009 with improved content. Moss is also a supporter of the
      <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">
       UK Independence Party
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Quotes">
       Quotes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Quotes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2130" data-file-width="1420" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg/220px-Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg/330px-Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg/440px-Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stirling_Moss_2014_2_amk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Moss in 2014
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      "I certainly had an appreciation of the danger which to me was part of the pleasure of racing. To me now racing is  the dangers are taken away: if it's difficult, they put in a chicane. So really now the danger is minimal  which is good, because people aren't hurt. But for me the fact that I had danger on my shoulder made it much more exciting. It's rather like if you flirt with a girl, it's more exciting than paying for a prostitute, because while you know you're gonna get it, the other one you don't. And I think with driving a motor car, the danger is a very necessary ingredient. Like if you're cooking, you need salt. You can cook without salt, but it doesn't have the flavour. It's the same with motor racing without danger. For me."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       On older drivers
      </i>
      : "You don't know how many years they've driven causing accidents! I'm not quite as urgent as I was... I know that my knowledge of road signs, there's some that I might not know which I should know... The other thing I find as I get older I'm less inclined to check the oil and check the tyres and so on, which is very important."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Driving_ban">
       Driving ban
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Driving ban">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In April 1960, Moss was found guilty of
      <a href="/wiki/Dangerous_driving" title="Dangerous driving">
       dangerous driving
      </a>
      . He was fined 50 and banned from driving for twelve months after an incident near
      <a href="/wiki/Chetwynd,_Shropshire" title="Chetwynd, Shropshire">
       Chetwynd, Shropshire
      </a>
      when he was test-driving a
      <a href="/wiki/Mini" title="Mini">
       Mini
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ban_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ban-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">
       Controversy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Controversy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Gay rights campaigners criticized remarks Moss made in a 2013 interview at the Motor Racing Hall of Fame, saying they were "offensive" and "homophobic". Moss had said he would not want a "poofter or anything like that" to play him on screen, and added that he thought "it would be difficult for someone of the other persuasion, who is homosexual, to take on the part, as I have spent my life driving cars and chasing girls." Responding to the criticism, he said: "Im sorry Ive caused offence, but Im disappointed anyone could be so narrow-minded as to take offence. It was not meant to cause any.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Later the same year Moss again caused controversy by saying that women "lacked the mental aptitude" to compete in Formula 1.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Racing_record">
       Racing record
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stirling_Moss&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Racing record">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Complete_Formula_One_World_Championship_results">
       Complete Formula One World Championship results
